I've uploaded a code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
oxlint(lsp): Auto-fix for unused eslint-disable directives should delete the line, not leave blank comments
### Confirm that this is a Bug for the editor extension, not the CLI

- [x] This bug does not happen in the Oxlint/Oxfmt CLI
- [x] After restarting the editor, the bug still appears

<!-- If you are able to see the same problem in the CLI, please report your issue at https://github.com/oxc-project/oxc -->

### Versions used

<!-- Please fill out the versions, hover over the Status Bar "oxc" in the bottom right to get the information as needed. -->

```
VS Code extension: v1.52.0
oxlint: v1.58.0
oxfmt: v0.43.0
VS Code version: 1.105.1
Operating System and Version: macOs 26.3.1
Node Version: v24.12.0
Node Manager: npm v11.6.2
```

### What happened?

When Oxlint reports an unused disable directive (e.g. with `reportUnusedDisableDirectives` enabled in the Oxlint config), the **CLI does not offer an auto-fix** for that diagnostic. The **VS Code extension** does apply a fix (e.g. via **Fix all** / `source.fixAll.oxc` on save), but the fix is **wrong**: it strips the directive text and leaves an **empty comment** on the line (`//` or `/**/`) instead of **removing the whole line**, which matches what users expect from ESLint-style tooling and leaves noisy, useless lines in the file.

**Steps to reproduce**
1. Clone https://github.com/arsnl/oxlint-repro-file-level-disable and open the folder in VS Code.
2. Run `npm install`.
3. In `.vscode/settings.json`, set `"source.fixAll.oxc"` to `"always"` under `editor.codeActionsOnSave` (or use **Fix all** from the lightbulb on an unused-disable diagnostic).
4. Save `test.ts` (or trigger fix all).
**Actual behavior:** Lines that contained only the disable comment become `//` or `/**/` with nothing after it.

**Expected behavior:** The **entire line** should be removed when nothing meaningful remains (same idea as removing a full `eslint-disable` line), not replaced with an empty comment token.
*(Related upstream context: in that repro, file-level `oxlint-disable` for a file-scope rule may still leave the real rule violation plus an “unused directive” warning—[that’s separate Oxlint engine behavior](https://github.com/oxc-project/oxc/issues/21072); this ticket is specifically about the **editor fix** leaving empty comments.)*

### Reproduction repo

https://github.com/arsnl/oxlint-repro-file-level-disable  

Minimal workspace: `test.ts`, `oxlint.config.ts` (`reportUnusedDisableDirectives: "warn"`), and `.vscode/` recommendations for `oxc.oxc-vscode`. See the **“Reproduction (VS Code extension)”** section in the repo `README.md`.

   325	        // relate to lint result, check after linter run finish

    11	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Eq, PartialEq)]
    12	enum DisabledRule {
    13	    /// Disables all linting rules for a span of code.
    14	    /// Used by directives like `eslint-disable`, `eslint-disable-next-line`, or `eslint-disable-line` without specific rule names.
    15	    ///
    16	    /// # Example
    17	    /// ```text
    18	    /// /* eslint-disable */
    19	    ///    ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^ comment_span
    20	    /// ```
    21	    All {
    22	        /// Span of the comment containing the disable directive
    23	        comment_span: Span,
    24	        /// Whether this is a line-specific directive (`-next-line` or `-line`).
    25	        is_next_line: bool,
    26	    },
    27	    /// Disables a single specific linting rule for a span of code.
    28	    /// Used by directives like `eslint-disable rule-name`, `eslint-disable-next-line rule-name`, or `eslint-disable-line rule-name`.
    29	    ///
    30	    /// # Example
    31	    /// ```text
    32	    /// /* eslint-disable no-debugger */
    33	    ///   ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^ comment_span
    34	    ///                   ^^^^^^^^^^^  name_span (for "no-debugger")
    35	    /// ```
    36	    Single {
    37	        /// Name of the disabled rule (e.g., "no-debugger", "no-console")
    38	        rule_name: String,
    39	        /// Span of the rule name within the comment.
    40	        ///
    41	        /// For `/* eslint-disable no-debugger */`, this points to "no-debugger".
    42	        name_span: Span,
    43	        /// Span of the entire comment content containing the disable directive.
    44	        ///
    45	        /// For `/* eslint-disable no-debugger */`, this points to "eslint-disable no-debugger".
    46	        comment_span: Span,
    47	        /// Whether this is a line-specific directive (`-next-line` or `-line`).
    48	        /// When true, only diagnostics starting within the interval are suppressed.
    49	        /// When false, any diagnostic overlapping the interval is suppressed.
    50	        is_next_line: bool,
    51	    },
    52	}
    53	
    54	impl DisabledRule {
    55	    pub fn comment_span(&self) -> &Span {
    56	        match self {
    57	            DisabledRule::All { comment_span, .. } | DisabledRule::Single { comment_span, .. } => {
    58	                comment_span
    59	            }
    60	        }
    61	    }
    62	
    63	    pub fn is_next_line(&self) -> bool {
    64	        match self {
    65	            DisabledRule::All { is_next_line, .. } | DisabledRule::Single { is_next_line, .. } => {
    66	                *is_next_line
    67	            }
    68	        }
    69	    }
    70	}

    94	impl RuleCommentRule {
    95	    #[expect(clippy::cast_possible_truncation)] // for `as u32`
    96	    pub fn create_fix(&self, source_text: &str, comment_span: Span) -> Fix {
    97	        let before_source =
    98	            &source_text[comment_span.start as usize..self.name_span.start as usize];
    99	
   100	        // check if there is a comma before the rule name
   101	        // if there is, remove the comma, whitespace and the rule name
   102	        let mut comma_before_offset = None;
   103	        for (i, c) in before_source.chars().rev().enumerate() {
   104	            if c.is_whitespace() {
   105	                continue;
   106	            }
   107	            if c == ',' {
   108	                comma_before_offset = Some(1 + i as u32);
   109	            }
   110	            break;
   111	        }
   112	
   113	        if let Some(comma_before_offset) = comma_before_offset {
   114	            return Fix::delete(Span::new(
   115	                self.name_span.start - comma_before_offset,
   116	                self.name_span.end,
   117	            ))
   118	            .with_kind(FixKind::Suggestion);
   119	        }
   120	
   121	        let after_source = &source_text[self.name_span.end as usize..comment_span.end as usize];
   122	
   123	        // check if there is a comma after the rule name
   124	        // if there is, remove the comma, whitespace and the rule name
   125	        let mut comma_after_offset = None;
   126	        for (i, c) in after_source.char_indices() {
   127	            if c.is_whitespace() {
   128	                continue;
   129	            }
   130	            if c == ',' {
   131	                comma_after_offset = Some(1 + i as u32);
   132	            }
   133	            break;
   134	        }
   135	
   136	        if let Some(comma_after_offset) = comma_after_offset {
   137	            return Fix::delete(Span::new(
   138	                self.name_span.start,
   139	                self.name_span.end + comma_after_offset,
   140	            ))
   141	            .with_kind(FixKind::Suggestion);
   142	        }
   143	
   144	        unreachable!(
   145	            "A `RuleCommentRule` should have a comma, because only one rule should be RuleCommentType::All"
   146	        );
   147	    }
   148	}

   235	    /// At the moment, this only handles changes to lint configuration files
   236	    /// When a change is detected, the linter is refreshed and all diagnostics are revalidated
   237	    pub async fn did_change_watched_files(
   238	        &self,
   239	        file_event: &FileEvent,
   240	        needs_diagnostic_refresh: &mut bool,
   241	        file_system: Option<&LSPFileSystem>,

   243	        // Diagnostic reports that need to be revalidated
   244	        Option<Vec<(Uri, Vec<Diagnostic>)>>,

   247	        // Watchers that need to be unregistered

   250	        // Scope the first lock so it is dropped before the second lock

   253	            options_guard.clone().unwrap_or_default()

   267	    /// Handle server configuration changes from the client
   268	    ///
   269	    /// # Panics
   270	    /// Panics if the root URI cannot be converted to a file path.
   271	    pub async fn did_change_configuration(
   272	        &self,
   273	        changed_options_json: serde_json::Value,
   274	        needs_diagnostic_refresh: &mut bool,
   275	        file_system: Option<&LSPFileSystem>,
   276	    ) -> (
   277	        // Diagnostic reports that need to be revalidated
   278	        Option<Vec<(Uri, Vec<Diagnostic>)>>,
   279	        // New watchers that need to be registered
   280	        Vec<Registration>,
   281	        // Watchers that need to be unregistered
   282	        Vec<Unregistration>,
   283	    ) {
   284	        // Scope the first lock so it is dropped before the second lock
   285	        let old_options = {
   286	            let options_guard = self.options.lock().await;
   287	            options_guard.clone().unwrap_or_default()
   288	        };
   289	        debug!(
   290	            "
   291	        configuration changed:
   292	        incoming: {changed_options_json:?}
   293	        current: {old_options:?}
   294	        "
   295	        );
   296	
   297	        let result = self
   298	            .handle_tool_changes(file_system, needs_diagnostic_refresh, |tool, builder| {
   299	                tool.handle_configuration_change(
   300	                    builder,
   301	                    &self.root_uri,
   302	                    &old_options,

   304	                )
   305	            })
   306	            .await;
   307	
   308	        {
   309	            let mut options_guard = self.options.lock().await;
   310	            *options_guard = Some(changed_options_json);
   311	        }
   312	
   313	        result
   314	    }

   501	            watch_patterns: None,

   504	
   505	    /// Tries to execute the given command with the provided arguments.
   506	    /// If the command is not recognized, returns `Err(ErrorCode)`.
   507	    /// If the command is recognized and executed it can return:
   508	    /// - `Ok(Some(WorkspaceEdit))` if the command was executed successfully and produced a workspace edit.
   509	    /// - `Ok(None)` if the command was executed successfully but did not produce any workspace edit.
   510	    ///
   511	    /// # Errors
   512	    /// Returns an `ErrorCode::InvalidParams` if the command arguments are invalid.
   513	    fn execute_command(
   514	        &self,
   515	        command: &str,
   516	        arguments: Vec<serde_json::Value>,
   517	    ) -> Result<Option<WorkspaceEdit>, ErrorCode> {
   518	        if command != FIX_ALL_COMMAND_ID {
   519	            return Err(ErrorCode::InvalidParams);
   520	        }
   521	
   522	        let args = FixAllCommandArgs::try_from(arguments).map_err(|_| ErrorCode::InvalidParams)?;
   523	        let uri: Uri = args.uri.parse().map_err(|_| ErrorCode::InvalidParams)?;
   524	
   525	        if !self.is_responsible_for_uri(&uri) {
   526	            return Ok(None);
   527	        }
   528	
   529	        let actions = self.get_code_actions_for_uri(&uri, Some(CodeActionTriggerKind::INVOKED));
   530	
   531	        let Some(actions) = actions else {
   532	            return Ok(None);
   533	        };
   534	
   535	        if actions.is_empty() {
   536	            return Ok(None);
   537	        }
   538	
   539	        let text_edits = fix_all_text_edit(actions.into_iter());
   540	
   541	        Ok(Some(WorkspaceEdit {
   542	            #[expect(clippy::disallowed_types)]
   543	            changes: Some(std::collections::HashMap::from([(uri, text_edits)])),
   544	            document_changes: None,
   545	            change_annotations: None,
   546	        }))
   547	    }
   548	
   549	    fn get_code_actions_or_commands(
   550	        &self,
   551	        uri: &Uri,
   552	        range: &Range,
   553	        context: &CodeActionContext,
   554	    ) -> Vec<CodeActionOrCommand> {
   555	        let actions = self.get_code_actions_for_uri(uri, context.trigger_kind);
   556	
   557	        let Some(actions) = actions else {
   558	            return vec![];
   559	        };
   560	
   561	        if actions.is_empty() {
   562	            return vec![];
   563	        }
   564	
   565	        let actions = actions.into_iter().filter(|r| range_overlaps(*range, r.range));
   566	
   567	        // `context.only` is a special case here. ESLint behavior is if `source.fixAll` is the first element in `context.only`,
   568	        // then only return fix all code action, and ignore other code actions, even if they are requested.
   569	        // https://github.com/microsoft/vscode-eslint/blob/1572a25c619861a812c6593c9b130ee52361bcf0/server/src/eslintServer.ts#L587-L589
   570	        // This works for zed editor too, it sends always with this layout: `"only": ["quickfix", "source.fixAll.oxc", "source.fixAll"]`
   571	        // https://github.com/oxc-project/oxc-zed/issues/133#issuecomment-4007046920
   572	        // To align more with the official LSP specs, we implement it a bit differently:
   573	        // If no `context.only` is applied, only return the quick fix code actions.
   574	        // If it is provided, we should loop over it and return the actions in the same order.
   575	        // https://microsoft.github.io/language-server-protocol/specifications/lsp/3.17/specification/#codeActionContext
   576	        let applying_kinds = match &context.only {
   577	            Some(only) => {
   578	                // `source.fixAll` and `source.fixAll.oxc` should behave the same, filter duplicate out
   579	                let mut seen = FxHashSet::default();
   580	                only.iter()
   581	                    .filter_map(|kind| {
   582	                        if kind == &CODE_ACTION_KIND_SOURCE_FIX_ALL_OXC
   583	                            || kind == &CodeActionKind::SOURCE_FIX_ALL
   584	                        {
   585	                            if seen.contains(&CodeActionKind::SOURCE_FIX_ALL) {
   586	                                None
   587	                            } else {
   588	                                seen.insert(CodeActionKind::SOURCE_FIX_ALL);
   589	                                Some(CodeActionKind::SOURCE_FIX_ALL)
   590	                            }
   591	                        } else {
   592	                            Some(kind.clone())
   593	                        }
   594	                    })
   595	                    .collect::<Vec<_>>()
   596	            }
   597	            // if `only` is not provided, only return quickfixes
   598	            None => vec![CodeActionKind::QUICKFIX],
   599	        };
   600	
   601	        let mut code_actions_vec: Vec<CodeActionOrCommand> = vec![];
   602	
   603	        for kind in applying_kinds {
   604	            // `CODE_ACTION_KIND_SOURCE_FIX_ALL_OXC` was filtered out by `applying_kinds`, so we don't need to check it here.
   605	            if kind == CodeActionKind::SOURCE_FIX_ALL {
   606	                let Some(fix_all) = apply_all_fix_code_action(actions.clone(), uri.clone()) else {
   607	                    continue;
   608	                };
   609	                code_actions_vec.push(CodeActionOrCommand::CodeAction(fix_all));
   610	            } else if kind == CODE_ACTION_KIND_SOURCE_FIX_ALL_DANGEROUS_OXC {
   611	                if !self.fix_kind.is_dangerous() {
   612	                    warn!(
   613	                        "Linter is not configured to provide dangerous fixes. Please set `fixKind` to `dangerous_fix` or `dangerous_fix_or_suggestion` in the server configuration to enable it."
   614	                    );
   615	                    continue;
   616	                }
   617	                let Some(fix_all) = apply_dangerous_fix_code_action(actions.clone(), uri.clone())
   618	                else {
   619	                    continue;
   620	                };
   621	                code_actions_vec.push(CodeActionOrCommand::CodeAction(fix_all));
   622	            } else if kind == CodeActionKind::QUICKFIX {
   623	                for action in actions.clone() {
   624	                    let fix_actions = apply_fix_code_actions(action, uri);
   625	                    code_actions_vec
   626	                        .extend(fix_actions.into_iter().map(CodeActionOrCommand::CodeAction));
   627	                }
   628	            }
   629	        }
   630	
   631	        code_actions_vec
   632	    }
   633

   638	    }

    50	#[derive(Default)]
    51	pub struct ServerLinterBuilder {
    52	    external_linter: Option<ExternalLinter>,
    53	    #[cfg(feature = "napi")]
    54	    js_config_loader: Option<crate::js_config::JsConfigLoaderCb>,
    55	}
    56	
    57	impl ServerLinterBuilder {
    58	    pub fn new(
    59	        external_linter: Option<ExternalLinter>,
    60	        #[cfg(feature = "napi")] js_config_loader: Option<crate::js_config::JsConfigLoaderCb>,
    61	    ) -> Self {
    62	        Self {
    63	            external_linter,
    64	            #[cfg(feature = "napi")]
    65	            js_config_loader,
    66	        }
    67	    }
    68	
    69	    /// # Panics
    70	    /// Panics if the root URI cannot be converted to a file path.
    71	    pub fn build(&self, root_uri: &Uri, options: serde_json::Value) -> ServerLinter {
    72	        let options = match serde_json::from_value::<LSPLintOptions>(options) {
    73	            Ok(opts) => opts,
    74	            Err(e) => {
    75	                warn!(
    76	                    "Failed to deserialize LSPLintOptions from JSON: {e}. Falling back to default options."
    77	                );
    78	                LSPLintOptions::default()
    79	            }
    80	        };
    81	        let root_path = root_uri.to_file_path().unwrap();
    82	        let mut external_linter = self.external_linter.as_ref();
    83	        let mut external_plugin_store = ExternalPluginStore::new(external_linter.is_some());
    84	
    85	        // Setup JS workspace. This must be done before loading any configs
    86	        if let Some(external_linter) = external_linter {
    87	            let res = (external_linter.create_workspace)(root_uri.as_str().to_string());
    88	
    89	            if let Err(err) = res {
    90	                error!("Failed to setup JS workspace:\n{err}\n");
    91	            }
    92	        }
    93	
    94	        let config_path = options.config_path.as_ref().filter(|p| !p.is_empty()).map(PathBuf::from);
    95	        let loader = ConfigLoader::new(
    96	            external_linter,
    97	            &mut external_plugin_store,
    98	            &[],
    99	            Some(root_uri.as_str()),
   100	        );
   101	        #[cfg(feature = "napi")]
   102	        let loader = loader.with_js_config_loader(self.js_config_loader.as_ref());
   103	
   104	        let oxlintrc =
   105	            match loader.load_root_config_with_ancestor_search(&root_path, config_path.as_ref()) {
   106	                Ok(config) => config,
   107	                Err(e) => {
   108	                    warn!("Failed to load config: {e}");
   109	                    Oxlintrc::default()
   110	                }
   111	            };
   112	
   113	        let mut nested_ignore_patterns = Vec::new();

    43	pub fn apply_fix_code_actions(action: LinterCodeAction, uri: &Uri) -> Vec<CodeAction> {
    44	    let mut code_actions = vec![];
    45	
    46	    let mut preferred_possible = true;
    47	    for fixed in action.fixed_content {
    48	        // only rule fixes and unused directive fixes can be preferred, ignore fixes are not preferred.
    49	        let preferred = preferred_possible
    50	            && matches!(
    51	                fixed.lsp_kind,
    52	                FixedContentKind::LintRule | FixedContentKind::UnusedDirective
    53	            );
    54	        if preferred {
    55	            // only the first fix can be preferred, if there are multiple fixes available.
    56	            preferred_possible = false;
    57	        }
    58	        let action = fix_content_to_code_action(fixed, uri.clone(), preferred);
    59	        code_actions.push(action);
    60	    }
    61	
    62	    code_actions
    63	}

   116	
   117	/// Collect safe text edits from the provided diagnostic reports, which can be applied at once.
   118	pub fn fix_all_text_edit(actions: impl Iterator<Item = LinterCodeAction>) -> Vec<TextEdit> {
   119	    let mut text_edits: Vec<TextEdit> = vec![];
   120	
   121	    for action in actions {
   122	        // Applying all possible fixes at once is not possible in this context.
   123	        // Search for the first "real" fix for the rule, and ignore the rest of the fixes for the same rule.
   124	        let Some(fixed_content) = action.fixed_content.into_iter().find(|fixed| {
   125	            matches!(fixed.lsp_kind, FixedContentKind::LintRule | FixedContentKind::UnusedDirective)
   126	        }) else {
   127	            continue;
   128	        };
   129	
   130	        // Only safe fixes or suggestions are applied in "fix all" action/command.
   131	        if !FixKind::SafeFixOrSuggestion.can_apply(fixed_content.kind) {
   132	            debug!("Skipping unsafe fix for fix all action: {}", fixed_content.message);
   133	            continue;
   134	        }
   135	
   136	        text_edits.push(TextEdit { range: fixed_content.range, new_text: fixed_content.code });
   137	    }
   138	
   139	    // LSP spec requires text edits in a WorkspaceEdit to be non-overlapping.
   140	    // Sort by start position so adjacent fixes are applied in order, then drop
   141	    // any edit whose range overlaps (or touches) the previous one via range_overlaps.
   142	    text_edits.sort_unstable_by(|a, b| {
   143	        a.range
   144	            .start
   145	            .line
   146	            .cmp(&b.range.start.line)
   147	            .then(a.range.start.character.cmp(&b.range.start.character))
   148	    });
   149	
   150	    let mut result: Vec<TextEdit> = Vec::with_capacity(text_edits.len());
   151	    for edit in text_edits {
   152	        if let Some(last) = result.last()
   153	            && range_overlaps(last.range, edit.range)
   154	        {
   155	            debug!("Skipping overlapping fix at {:?}", edit.range);
   156	            continue;
   157	        }
   158	        result.push(edit);
   159	    }
   160	    result
   161	}
   162	
   163	fn dangerous_fix_all_text_edit(actions: impl Iterator<Item = LinterCodeAction>) -> Vec<TextEdit> {
   164	    let mut text_edits: Vec<TextEdit> = vec![];
   165	
   166	    for action in actions {
   167	        let Some(fixed_content) = action.fixed_content.into_iter().find(|fixed| {
   168	            matches!(fixed.lsp_kind, FixedContentKind::LintRule | FixedContentKind::UnusedDirective)
   169	        }) else {
   170	            continue;
   171	        };
   172	
   173	        text_edits.push(TextEdit { range: fixed_content.range, new_text: fixed_content.code });
   174	    }
   175	
   176	    text_edits
   177	}

   210	    #[test]
   211	    fn test_fix_all_text_edit_sorts_by_position() {
   212	        // Edits provided in reverse order should be sorted by start position.
   213	        let actions = vec![make_ranged_action(2, 0, 2, 5), make_ranged_action(0, 0, 0, 5)];
   214	        let result = fix_all_text_edit(actions.into_iter());
   215	        assert_eq!(result.len(), 2);
   216	        assert_eq!(result[0].range.start.line, 0);
   217	        assert_eq!(result[1].range.start.line, 2);
   218	    }
   219	
   220	    #[test]
   221	    fn test_fix_all_text_edit_drops_overlapping() {
   222	        // The second edit overlaps the first; only the first should be kept.
   223	        let actions = vec![make_ranged_action(0, 0, 0, 10), make_ranged_action(0, 5, 0, 15)];
   224	        let result = fix_all_text_edit(actions.into_iter());
   225	        assert_eq!(result.len(), 1);
   226	        assert_eq!(result[0].range.end.character, 10);
   227	    }
   228	
   229	    #[test]
   230	    fn test_fix_all_text_edit_drops_adjacent_edits() {
   231	        // range_overlaps uses non-strict comparisons, so adjacent edits (where the end of one
   232	        // equals the start of the next) are conservatively treated as overlapping and the second
   233	        // is dropped. This is a safe trade-off: the fix can be applied on the next invocation,
   234	        // and it avoids any risk of producing unexpected output for boundary-sharing edits.
   235	        let actions = vec![make_ranged_action(0, 0, 0, 5), make_ranged_action(0, 5, 0, 10)];
   236	        let result = fix_all_text_edit(actions.into_iter());
   237	        assert_eq!(result.len(), 1);
   238	    }

    44	fn miette_severity_to_lsp_severity(value: Severity) -> DiagnosticSeverity {
    45	    match value {
    46	        Severity::Error => DiagnosticSeverity::ERROR,
    47	        Severity::Warning => DiagnosticSeverity::WARNING,
    48	        Severity::Advice => DiagnosticSeverity::HINT,
    49	    }
    50	}
    51	// clippy: the source field is checked and assumed to be less than 4GB, and
    52	// we assume that the fix offset will not exceed 2GB in either direction
    53	#[expect(clippy::cast_possible_truncation)]
    54	pub fn message_to_lsp_diagnostic(
    55	    message: Message,
    56	    uri: &Uri,
    57	    source_text: &str,
    58	    rope: &Rope,
    59	) -> DiagnosticReport {
    60	    let severity = miette_severity_to_lsp_severity(message.error.severity);
    61	
    62	    let related_information = message.error.labels.as_ref().map(|spans| {
    63	        spans
    64	            .iter()
    65	            .map(|span| {
    66	                let offset = span.offset() as u32;
    67	                let start_position = offset_to_position(rope, offset, source_text);
    68	                let end_position =
    69	                    offset_to_position(rope, offset + span.len() as u32, source_text);
    70	
    71	                ls_types::DiagnosticRelatedInformation {
    72	                    location: ls_types::Location {
    73	                        uri: uri.clone(),
    74	                        range: ls_types::Range::new(start_position, end_position),
    75	                    },
    76	                    message: span
    77	                        .label()
    78	                        .map_or_else(String::new, std::string::ToString::to_string),
    79	                }
    80	            })
    81	            .collect()
    82	    });
    83	
    84	    let start_position = offset_to_position(rope, message.span.start, source_text);
    85	    let end_position = offset_to_position(rope, message.span.end, source_text);
    86	    let range = Range::new(start_position, end_position);
    87	
    88	    let code = message.error.code.to_string();
    89	    let code_description = message
    90	        .error
    91	        .url
    92	        .as_ref()
    93	        .and_then(|url| url.parse().ok())
    94	        .map(|href| CodeDescription { href });
    95	
    96	    let mut diagnostic_message = String::with_capacity(
    97	        message.error.message.len()
    98	            + message.error.help.as_ref().map_or(0, |h| h.len() + 7) // "help: " prefix
    99	            + message.error.note.as_ref().map_or(0, |n| n.len() + 7), // "note: " prefix
   100	    );
   101	
   102	    diagnostic_message.push_str(&message.error.message);
   103	    if let Some(help) = &message.error.help {
   104	        diagnostic_message.push_str("\nhelp: ");
   105	        diagnostic_message.push_str(help);
   106	    }
   107	
   108	    if let Some(note) = &message.error.note {
   109	        diagnostic_message.push_str("\nnote: ");
   110	        diagnostic_message.push_str(note);
   111	    }
   112	
   113	    // 1) Use `fixed_content.message` if it exists
   114	    // 2) Try to parse the report diagnostic message
   115	    // 3) Fallback to "Fix this problem"
   116	    let alternative_fix_title: Cow<'static, str> =
   117	        if let Some(code) = message.error.message.split(':').next() {
   118	            format!("Fix this {code} problem").into()
   119	        } else {
   120	            std::borrow::Cow::Borrowed("Fix this problem")
   121	        };
   122	
   123	    let diagnostic = Diagnostic {
   124	        range,
   125	        severity: Some(severity),
   126	        code: Some(NumberOrString::String(code)),
   127	        message: diagnostic_message,
   128	        source: Some("oxc".into()),
   129	        code_description,
   130	        related_information,
   131	        tags: None,
   132	        data: None,
   133	    };
   134	
   135	    let mut fixed_content = vec![];
   136	    // Convert PossibleFixes directly to PossibleFixContent
   137	    match message.fixes {
   138	        PossibleFixes::None => {}
   139	        PossibleFixes::Single(mut fix) => {
   140	            if fix.message.is_none() {
   141	                fix.message = Some(alternative_fix_title);
   142	            }
   143	            fixed_content.push(fix_to_fixed_content(
   144	                &fix,
   145	                rope,
   146	                source_text,
   147	                FixedContentKind::LintRule,
   148	            ));
   149	        }
   150	        PossibleFixes::Multiple(fixes) => {
   151	            fixed_content.extend(fixes.into_iter().map(|mut fix| {
   152	                if fix.message.is_none() {
   153	                    fix.message = Some(alternative_fix_title.clone());
   154	                }
   155	                fix_to_fixed_content(&fix, rope, source_text, FixedContentKind::LintRule)
   156	            }));
   157	        }
   158	    }
   159	
   160	    // Add ignore fixes
   161	    let error_offset = message.span.start;
   162	    let section_offset = message.section_offset;
   163	
   164	    // If the error is exactly at the section offset and has 0 span length, it means that the file is the problem
   165	    // and attaching a ignore comment would not ignore the error.
   166	    // This is because the ignore comment would need to be placed before the error offset, which is not possible.
   167	    if error_offset == section_offset && message.span.end == section_offset {
   168	        return DiagnosticReport {
   169	            diagnostic,
   170	            code_action: Some(LinterCodeAction { range, fixed_content }),
   171	        };
   172	    }
   173	
   174	    add_ignore_fixes(
   175	        &mut fixed_content,
   176	        &message.error.code,
   177	        error_offset,
   178	        section_offset,
   179	        rope,
   180	        source_text,
   181	    );
   182	
   183	    let code_action = if fixed_content.is_empty() {
   184	        None
   185	    } else {
   186	        Some(LinterCodeAction { range, fixed_content })
   187	    };
   188	
   189	    DiagnosticReport { diagnostic, code_action }
   190	}
   191	
   192	fn fix_to_fixed_content(
   193	    fix: &Fix,
   194	    rope: &Rope,
   195	    source_text: &str,
   196	    fix_kind: FixedContentKind,
   197	) -> FixedContent {
   198	    let start_position = offset_to_position(rope, fix.span.start, source_text);
   199	    let end_position = offset_to_position(rope, fix.span.end, source_text);
   200	
   201	    debug_assert!(
   202	        fix.message.is_some(),
   203	        "Fix message should be present. `message_to_lsp_diagnostic` should modify fixes to include messages."
   204	    );
   205	
   206	    FixedContent {
   207	        message: fix.message.as_ref().map(std::string::ToString::to_string).unwrap_or_default(),
   208	        code: fix.content.to_string(),
   209	        range: Range::new(start_position, end_position),
   210	        kind: fix.kind,
   211	        lsp_kind: fix_kind,
   212	    }
   213	}
   214	
   215	pub fn generate_inverted_diagnostics(
   216	    diagnostics: &[DiagnosticReport],
   217	    uri: &Uri,
   218	) -> Vec<DiagnosticReport> {
   219	    let mut inverted_diagnostics = vec![];
   220	    for d in diagnostics {
   221	        let Some(related_info) = &d.diagnostic.related_information else {
   222	            continue;
   223	        };
   224	        let related_information = Some(vec![DiagnosticRelatedInformation {
   225	            location: ls_types::Location { uri: uri.clone(), range: d.diagnostic.range },
   226	            message: "original diagnostic".to_string(),
   227	        }]);
   228	        for r in related_info {
   229	            if r.location.range == d.diagnostic.range {
   230	                continue;
   231	            }
   232	            // If there is no message content for this span, then don't produce an additional diagnostic
   233	            // which also has no content. This prevents issues where editors expect diagnostics to have messages.
   234	            if r.message.is_empty() {
   235	                continue;
   236	            }
   237	            inverted_diagnostics.push(DiagnosticReport {
   238	                diagnostic: Diagnostic {
   239	                    range: r.location.range,
   240	                    severity: Some(DiagnosticSeverity::HINT),
   241	                    code: None,
   242	                    message: r.message.clone(),
   243	                    source: d.diagnostic.source.clone(),
   244	                    code_description: None,
   245	                    related_information: related_information.clone(),
   246	                    tags: None,
   247	                    data: None,
   248	                },
   249	                code_action: None,
   250	            });
   251	        }
   252	    }
   253	    inverted_diagnostics
   254	}

   257	pub fn create_unused_directives_report(
   258	    directives: &DisableDirectives,
   259	    severity: AllowWarnDeny,
   260	    source_text: &str,
   261	    rope: &Rope,
   262	) -> Vec<DiagnosticReport> {

   264	    let fix_message = "remove unused disable directive";
   265	
   266	    let severity = if severity == AllowWarnDeny::Deny {
   267	        DiagnosticSeverity::ERROR
   268	    } else {
   269	        DiagnosticSeverity::WARNING
   270	    };
   271	
   272	    // Report unused disable comments
   273	    let unused_disable = directives.collect_unused_disable_comments();
   274	    for unused_comment in unused_disable {
   275	        let span = unused_comment.span;
   276	        match unused_comment.r#type {

   281	                    severity,
   282	                    source_text,
   283	                    rope,
   284	                    Some(&Fix::delete(span).with_message(fix_message)),
   285	                ));
   286	            }

   288	                for rule in rules {
   289	                    reports.push(build_unused_disable_diagnostic_report(
   290	                        format!(
   291	                            "Unused oxlint-disable directive (no problems were reported from {}).",
   292	                            rule.rule_name
   293	                        ),

   295	                        severity,
   296	                        source_text,
   297	                        rope,

   299	                    ));
   300	                }
   301	            }
   302	        }
   303	    }
   304	
   305	    // Report unused enable comments
   306	    let unused_enable = directives.unused_enable_comments();

   311	            )
   312	        } else {
   313	            "Unused oxlint-enable directive (no matching oxlint-disable directives were found)."
   314	                .to_string()

   322	            // TODO: fixer

   325	        ));

   373	fn prefix_to_plugin_name(prefix: &str) -> &str {
   374	    match prefix {
   375	        "eslint-plugin-import" => "import",
   376	        "eslint-plugin-jest" => "jest",
   377	        "eslint-plugin-jsdoc" => "jsdoc",
   378	        "eslint-plugin-jsx-a11y" => "jsx_a11y",

   385	        "eslint-plugin-vitest" => "vitest",
   386	        "eslint-plugin-node" => "node",
   387	        "eslint-plugin-vue" => "vue",

   424	            section_offset,

   426	            source_text,

   429	            &rule_name_with_plugin,

   249	
   250	    pub fn collect_unused_disable_comments(&self) -> Vec<DisableRuleComment> {
   251	        let used = self.used_disable_comments.borrow();
   252	
   253	        self.intervals
   254	            .iter()
   255	            // 1. group intervals with the same interval.val.comment_span() together
   256	            .chunk_by(|interval| interval.val.comment_span())
   257	            .into_iter()
   258	            // 2. iterate over all groups
   259	            // 3. check if the group has only one , ore all entries with the comment span are used with `used.contains(&interval.val))`
   260	            // 4. if all entries are used, map to RuleCommentType::All comment, otherwise map to RuleCommentType::Single comment.
   261	            .filter_map(|(comment_span, group)| {
   262	                let group_vec: Vec<_> = group.collect();
   263	
   264	                if group_vec.is_empty() {
   265	                    return None;
   266	                }
   267	
   268	                let rules: Vec<RuleCommentRule> = group_vec
   269	                    .iter()
   270	                    .filter_map(|interval| {
   271	                        if used.contains(&interval.val) {
   272	                            return None;
   273	                        }
   274	                        match &interval.val {
   275	                            DisabledRule::Single { rule_name, name_span, .. } => {
   276	                                Some(RuleCommentRule {
   277	                                    rule_name: rule_name.clone(),
   278	                                    name_span: *name_span,
   279	                                })
   280	                            }
   281	                            DisabledRule::All { .. } => Some(RuleCommentRule {
   282	                                rule_name: "all".to_string(),
   283	                                name_span: *comment_span,
   284	                            }),
   285	                        }
   286	                    })
   287	                    .collect::<Vec<_>>();
   288	
   289	                if rules.is_empty() {
   290	                    return None;
   291	                }
   292	
   293	                if rules.len() == group_vec.len() {
   294	                    return Some(DisableRuleComment {
   295	                        span: *comment_span,
   296	                        r#type: RuleCommentType::All,
   297	                    });
   298	                }
   299	
   300	                Some(DisableRuleComment {
   301	                    span: *comment_span,
   302	                    r#type: RuleCommentType::Single(rules),
   303	                })
   304	            })
   305	            .collect()
   306	    }
   307	}

   348	    #[expect(clippy::cast_possible_truncation)] // for `as u32`
   349	    fn build_impl(&mut self, source_text: &str, comments: &[Comment]) {
   350	        let source_len = source_text.len() as u32;
   351	        // This algorithm iterates through the comments and builds all intervals
   352	        // for matching disable and enable pairs.
   353	        // Wrongly ordered matching pairs are not taken into consideration.
   354	
   355	        // NOTE: oxlint apply directive's logic not exactly same to eslint
   356	        // only `disable-all` & `enable-all`, or `disable-rule` & `enable-rule` will add to intervals for disable directives
   357	        // `disable-all` & `enable-rule` -> lone `disable-all` (enable-rule find not disable-rule before itself)
   358	        // https://github.com/eslint/eslint/blob/f67d5e875324a9d899598b11807a9c7624021432/lib/linter/apply-disable-directives.js#L308
   359	
   360	        // enable directive keep the same logic for checking unused
   361	        let mut unused_enable_directives: Vec<(Option<String>, Span)> = vec![];
   362	
   363	        for comment in comments {
   364	            let comment_span = comment.content_span();
   365	            let text_source = comment_span.source_text(source_text);
   366	            let text = text_source.trim_start();
   367	            let mut rule_name_start = comment_span.start + (text_source.len() - text.len()) as u32;
   368	
   369	            if let Some(text) =
   370	                text.strip_prefix("eslint-disable").or_else(|| text.strip_prefix("oxlint-disable"))
   371	            {
   372	                rule_name_start += 14; // eslint-disable and oxlint-disable are each 14 bytes
   373	                // `eslint-disable`
   374	                if text.trim().is_empty() {
   375	                    if self.disable_all_start.is_none() {
   376	                        self.disable_all_start = Some((comment_span.end, comment_span));
   377	                    }
   378	                    self.disable_rule_comments.push(DisableRuleComment {
   379	                        span: comment_span,
   380	                        r#type: RuleCommentType::All,
   381	                    });
   382	                    continue;
   383	                }
   384	                // `eslint-disable-next-line`
   385	                else if let Some(text) = text.strip_prefix("-next-line") {
   386	                    rule_name_start += 10; // -next-line is 10 bytes
   387	                    // Get the span up to the next new line
   388	                    let mut stop = comment_span.end;
   389	                    let mut lines_after_comment_end =
   390	                        source_text[comment_span.end as usize..].split_inclusive('\n');
   391	
   392	                    if let Some(rest_of_line) = lines_after_comment_end.next() {
   393	                        stop += rest_of_line.len() as u32;
   394	                    }
   395	
   396	                    if let Some(next_line) = lines_after_comment_end.next() {
   397	                        let next_line_trimmed = next_line.trim_end_matches(['\n', '\r']);
   398	                        stop += next_line_trimmed.len() as u32;
   399	                    }
   400	
   401	                    if text.trim().is_empty() {
   402	                        self.add_interval(
   403	                            comment_span.end,
   404	                            stop,
   405	                            DisabledRule::All { comment_span, is_next_line: true },
   406	                        );
   407	                        self.disable_rule_comments.push(DisableRuleComment {
   408	                            span: comment_span,
   409	                            r#type: RuleCommentType::All,
   410	                        });
   411	                    } else {
   412	                        // `eslint-disable-next-line rule_name1, rule_name2`
   413	                        let mut rules = vec![];
   414	                        Self::get_rule_names(text, rule_name_start, |rule_name, name_span| {
   415	                            self.add_interval(
   416	                                comment_span.end,
   417	                                stop,
   418	                                DisabledRule::Single {
   419	                                    rule_name: rule_name.to_string(),
   420	                                    name_span,
   421	                                    comment_span,
   422	                                    is_next_line: true,
   423	                                },
   424	                            );
   425	                            rules.push(RuleCommentRule {
   426	                                rule_name: rule_name.to_string(),
   427	                                name_span,
   428	                            });
   429	                        });
   430	                        self.disable_rule_comments.push(DisableRuleComment {
   431	                            span: comment_span,
   432	                            r#type: RuleCommentType::Single(rules),
   433	                        });
   434	                    }
   435	                    continue;
   436	                }
   437	                // `eslint-disable-line`
   438	                else if let Some(text) = text.strip_prefix("-line") {
   439	                    rule_name_start += 5; // -line is 5 bytes
   440	
   441	                    // Get the span between the preceding newline to this comment
   442	                    let start = source_text[..comment_span.start as usize]
   443	                        .lines()
   444	                        .next_back()

   462	                        Self::get_rule_names(text, rule_name_start, |rule_name, name_span| {

   311	/// A completed, normalized fix ready to be applied to the source code.
   312	///
   313	/// Used internally by this module. Lint rules should use `RuleFix`.
   314	#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]
   315	#[non_exhaustive]
   316	pub struct Fix {
   317	    pub content: Cow<'static, str>,
   318	    /// A brief suggestion message describing the fix. Will be shown in
   319	    /// editors via code actions.
   320	    pub message: Option<Cow<'static, str>>,
   321	    pub kind: FixKind,
   322	    pub span: Span,
   323	}
   324	
   325	impl Default for Fix {
   326	    fn default() -> Self {
   327	        Self::empty()
   328	    }
   329	}
   330	
   331	impl Fix {
   332	    pub const fn delete(span: Span) -> Self {
   333	        Self { content: Cow::Borrowed(""), message: None, span, kind: FixKind::None }
   334	    }
   335	
   336	    pub fn new<T: Into<Cow<'static, str>>>(content: T, span: Span) -> Self {
   337	        Self { content: content.into(), message: None, span, kind: FixKind::None }
   338	    }
   339	
   340	    /// Creates a [`Fix`] that doesn't change the source code.
   341	    #[inline]
   342	    pub const fn empty() -> Self {
   343	        Self { content: Cow::Borrowed(""), message: None, span: SPAN, kind: FixKind::None }
   344	    }
   345	
   346	    #[must_use]
   347	    pub fn with_message(mut self, message: impl Into<Cow<'static, str>>) -> Self {
   348	        self.message = Some(message.into());
   349	        self
   350	    }

   353	    pub fn with_kind(mut self, kind: FixKind) -> Self {
   354	        self.kind = kind;

   356	    }

pub mod cli {
    pub use super::{command::*, init::*, lint::CliRunner, lsp::run_lsp, result::CliRunResult};
}

// Only include code to run linter when the `napi` feature is enabled.
// Without this, `tasks/website` will not compile on Linux or Windows.
// `tasks/website` depends on `oxlint` as a normal library, which causes linker errors if NAPI is enabled.
#[cfg(feature = "napi")]
mod js_config;
#[cfg(feature = "napi")]
mod run;
#[cfg(feature = "napi")]
pub use run::*;
use rustc_hash::FxHashSet;

// JS plugins are only supported on 64-bit little-endian platforms at present.
// Note: `raw_transfer_constants` module will not compile on 32-bit systems.
#[cfg(all(feature = "napi", target_pointer_width = "64", target_endian = "little"))]
mod generated {
    pub mod raw_transfer_constants;
}

#[cfg(all(feature = "napi", target_pointer_width = "64", target_endian = "little"))]
mod js_plugins;

// Use Mimalloc as the global allocator if `--features allocator` is enabled.
// Mimalloc has better performance, but this is feature-gated because it's slow to compile.
// `--features allocator` is only used in release builds.
#[cfg(all(
    feature = "allocator",
    not(any(
        target_arch = "arm",
        target_arch = "riscv64",
        miri,
        target_os = "freebsd",
        target_family = "wasm"
    ))
))]
#[global_allocator]
static GLOBAL: mimalloc_safe::MiMalloc = mimalloc_safe::MiMalloc;

const DEFAULT_OXLINTRC_NAME: &str = ".oxlintrc.json";
const DEFAULT_JSONC_OXLINTRC_NAME: &str = ".oxlintrc.jsonc";
const DEFAULT_TS_OXLINTRC_NAME: &str = "oxlint.config.ts";
/// Vite config file that may contain oxlint config under a `.lint` field.
const VITE_CONFIG_NAME: &str = "vite.config.ts";

/// Return a JSON blob containing metadata for all available oxlint rules.
///
/// This uses the internal JSON output formatter to generate the full list.
///
/// # Panics
/// Panics if the JSON generation fails, which should never happen under normal circumstances.
pub fn get_all_rules_json() -> String {
    use crate::output_formatter::{OutputFormat, OutputFormatter};

    OutputFormatter::new(OutputFormat::Json)
        .all_rules(FxHashSet::default())
        .expect("Failed to generate rules JSON")
}

   720	    fn is_ignored(&self, uri_path: &Path) -> bool {
   721	        if !Self::is_lintable_extension(uri_path) {
   722	            debug!("ignored (unsupported extension): {uri_path:?}");
   723	            return true;
   724	        }
   725	
   726	        if self.ignore_matcher.should_ignore(uri_path) {
   727	            debug!("ignored: {uri_path:?}");
   728	            return true;
   729	        }
   730	
   731	        for gitignore in &self.gitignore_glob {
   732	            if !uri_path.starts_with(gitignore.path()) {
   733	                continue;
   734	            }
   735	            if gitignore.matched_path_or_any_parents(uri_path, uri_path.is_dir()).is_ignore() {
   736	                debug!("ignored: {uri_path:?}");
   737	                return true;
   738	            }
   739	        }
   740	        false
   741	    }
   742	
   743	    /// Lint a single file, returning an empty diagnostics list if the file is ignored.
   744	    fn run_file(&self, uri: &Uri, content: Option<&str>) -> Result<Vec<Diagnostic>, String> {
   745	        let Some(uri_path) = uri.to_file_path() else {
   746	            return Ok(Vec::new());
   747	        };
   748	        if self.is_ignored(&uri_path) {
   749	            return Ok(Vec::new());
   750	        }
   751	
   752	        let reports = self.lint_path(&uri_path, uri, content)?;
   753	
   754	        let mut diagnostics = Vec::with_capacity(reports.len());
   755	        // mostly all diagnostics will have code actions (fix + ignoring line/file), only following diagnostics won't:
   756	        // - inverted diagnostics (related spans for the diagnostics)
   757	        // - diagnostics with span(0,0) and no fixes
   758	        // - tsgolint internal diagnostics
   759	        // - unused directives diagnostics
   760	        let mut code_actions = vec![];
   761	        for report in reports {
   762	            diagnostics.push(report.diagnostic);
   763	
   764	            if let Some(code_action) = report.code_action {
   765	                code_actions.push(code_action);
   766	            }
   767	        }
   768	
   769	        self.code_actions.pin().insert(uri.clone(), Some(code_actions));
   770	
   771	        Ok(diagnostics)
   772	    }
   773	
   774	    fn lint_path(
   775	        &self,
   776	        path: &Path,
   777	        uri: &Uri,
   778	        content: Option<&str>,
   779	    ) -> Result<Vec<DiagnosticReport>, String> {
   780	        debug!("lint {}", path.display());
   781	
   782	        let source_text = if let Some(content) = content {
   783	            content
   784	        } else {
   785	            &read_to_string(path).map_err(|e| format!("Failed to read file: {e}"))?
   786	        };
   787	
   788	        let rope = &Rope::from_str(source_text);
   789	
   790	        let mut fs = LspFileSystem::default();
   791	        fs.add_file(path.to_path_buf(), Arc::from(source_text));
   792	
   793	        let mut messages: Vec<DiagnosticReport> =
   794	            match self.runner.run_source(&[Arc::from(path.as_os_str())], &fs) {
   795	                Ok(results) => results
   796	                    .into_iter()
   797	                    .map(|message| message_to_lsp_diagnostic(message, uri, source_text, rope))
   798	                    .collect(),
   799	                Err(e) => {
   800	                    // clear disable directives on error to prevent stale directives
   801	                    self.runner.directives_coordinator().remove(path);
   802	                    return Err(e);
   803	                }
   804	            };
   805	
   806	        messages.append(&mut generate_inverted_diagnostics(&messages, uri));
   807	
   808	        // Add unused directives if configured
   809	        if let Some(severity) = self.unused_directives_severity
   810	            && let Some(directives) = self.runner.directives_coordinator().get(path)
   811	        {
   812	            messages.extend(create_unused_directives_report(
   813	                &directives,
   814	                severity,
   815	                source_text,
   816	                rope,
   817	            ));
   818	        }
   819	
   820	        // Clear any stale directives because they are no longer needed.
   821	        // This prevents using outdated directive spans if the new linting run fails.
   822	        self.runner.directives_coordinator().remove(path);
   823	
   824	        Ok(messages)
   825	    }

   206	    /// Given a relative file path (relative to `oxc_language_server` crate root), run the linter
   207	    /// and return the resulting diagnostics in a custom snapshot format.
   208	    pub fn test_and_snapshot_single_file(&self, relative_file_path: &str) {
   209	        self.test_and_snapshot_multiple_file(&[relative_file_path]);
   210	    }
   211	
   212	    pub fn get_file_uri(&self, relative_file_path: &str) -> Uri {
   213	        get_file_uri(&format!("{}/{}", self.relative_root_dir, relative_file_path))
   214	    }
   215	
   216	    pub fn test_and_snapshot_multiple_file(&self, relative_file_paths: &[&str]) {
   217	        let mut snapshot_result = String::new();
   218	        let context = CodeActionContext::default();
   219	        let fix_all_context = CodeActionContext {
   220	            only: Some(vec![CodeActionKind::SOURCE_FIX_ALL]),
   221	            ..Default::default()
   222	        };
   223	        for relative_file_path in relative_file_paths {
   224	            let uri = self.get_file_uri(relative_file_path);
   225	            let linter = self.create_linter();
   226	            let range = Range::new(Position::new(0, 0), Position::new(u32::MAX, u32::MAX));
   227	            let reports = FileResult {
   228	                diagnostic: linter.run_diagnostic(&TextDocument::new(
   229	                    &uri,
   230	                    oxc_language_server::LanguageId::default(),
   231	                    None,
   232	                )),
   233	                actions: linter.get_code_actions_or_commands(&uri, &range, &context),
   234	                fix_all_action: linter
   235	                    .get_code_actions_or_commands(&uri, &range, &fix_all_context)
   236	                    .into_iter()
   237	                    .next(),
   238	            };
   239	
   240	            let _ = write!(
   241	                snapshot_result,
   242	                "########## \nLinted file: {}/{relative_file_path}\n----------\n{}\n",
   243	                self.relative_root_dir,
   244	                get_snapshot_from_report(&reports)
   245	            );
   246	        }
   247	
   248	        #[expect(clippy::disallowed_methods)]
   249	        let snapshot_name = self.relative_root_dir.replace('/', "_");
   250	        let mut settings = insta::Settings::clone_current();
   251	        settings.set_prepend_module_to_snapshot(false);
   252	        settings.set_omit_expression(true);
   253	        #[expect(clippy::disallowed_methods)]
   254	        settings.set_snapshot_suffix(relative_file_paths.join("_").replace('\\', "/"));
   255	        settings.bind(|| {
   256	            insta::assert_snapshot!(snapshot_name, snapshot_result);
   257	        });
   258	    }

# Reproduce current LSP fix behavior for a standalone unused disable directive.
# The LSP currently receives a content span (inside comment delimiters) and turns
# it directly into a deletion edit, which leaves empty comment tokens.

def apply_delete(src, start, end):
    return src[:start] + src[end:]

cases = [
    ("// oxlint-disable no-console\nvar x = 'y';", 2, len("// oxlint-disable no-console")),
    ("/* oxlint-disable no-console */\nvar x = 'y';", 2, len("/* oxlint-disable no-console") - 2),
]

    13	    /// Flags describing an automatic code fix.
    14	    ///
    15	    /// These are used by lint rules when they provide a code fix or suggestion.
    16	    /// These are also used by the `LintService` to decide which kinds of
    17	    /// changes to apply.
    18	    ///
    19	    /// [`FixKind`] is designed to be interoperable with [`bool`]. `true` turns
    20	    /// into [`FixKind::Fix`] (applies only safe fixes) and `false` turns into
    21	    /// [`FixKind::None`] (do not apply any fixes or suggestions).
    22	    #[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash)]
    23	    pub struct FixKind: u8 {
    24	        /// An automatic code fix. Most of these are applied with `--fix`
    25	        ///
    26	        const Fix = 1 << 0;
    27	        /// A recommendation about how to fix a rule violation. These are usually
    28	        /// safe to apply, in that they shouldn't cause parse or runtime errors,
    29	        /// but may change the meaning of the code.
    30	        const Suggestion = 1 << 1;
    31	        /// Marks a fix or suggestion as dangerous. Dangerous fixes/suggestions
    32	        /// may break the code. Covers cases that are
    33	        /// - Aggressive (e.g. some code removal)
    34	        /// - Are under development. Think of this as similar to the `nursery`
    35	        ///   rule category.
    36	        const Dangerous = 1 << 2;
    37	
    38	        const SafeFix = Self::Fix.bits();
    39	        const SafeFixOrSuggestion = Self::Fix.bits() | Self::Suggestion.bits();
    40	        const DangerousFix = Self::Dangerous.bits() | Self::Fix.bits();
    41	        const DangerousSuggestion = Self::Dangerous.bits() | Self::Suggestion.bits();
    42	        const DangerousFixOrSuggestion = Self::Dangerous.bits() | Self::Fix.bits() | Self::Suggestion.bits();
    43	
    44	        /// Used to specify that no fixes should be applied.
    45	        const None = 0;
    46	        /// Fixes and Suggestions that are safe or dangerous.
    47	        const All = Self::Dangerous.bits() | Self::Fix.bits() | Self::Suggestion.bits();
    48	    }

    76	    /// to the source code.
    77	    ///
    78	    /// Here, `self` is the set of allowed [`FixKind`]s, and `rule_fix` is the
    79	    /// kind of fixed produced by the rule.
    80	    ///
    81	    /// # Example
    82	    /// ```
    83	    /// use oxc_linter::FixKind;
    84	    ///
    85	    /// // `none` means no fixes will be applied at all

/// Create a deletion fix for an unused disable directive.
///
/// Disable directive spans point at the comment content (for example, the
/// `oxlint-disable ...` part of `// oxlint-disable ...`). Deleting that span
/// directly leaves behind empty comment delimiters (`//` or `/**/`). When the
/// directive is the only meaningful content on its line, expand the fix to the
/// whole line so editor fix-all removes the noisy empty comment entirely.
fn unused_directive_delete_fix(source_text: &str, span: Span) -> Fix {
    let start = span.start as usize;
    let end = span.end as usize;

    let line_start = source_text[..start].rfind('"'"'\n'"'"').map_or(0, |index| index + 1);
    let line_end = source_text[end..]
        .find('"'"'\n'"'"')
        .map_or(source_text.len(), |index| end + index);

    let line_before_directive = &source_text[line_start..start];
    let line_after_directive = &source_text[end..line_end];

    // If the only non-whitespace tokens outside the directive span are comment
    // delimiters, removing just the directive would leave an empty comment.
    // Expand to the entire line in that case. Keep the newline (if any) so
    // deleting the first line doesn'"'"'t merge the following line into it.
    let is_standalone_comment = line_before_directive
        .trim_start_matches(char::is_whitespace)
        .trim_end()
        == "//"
        && line_after_directive.trim().is_empty()
        || line_before_directive
            .trim_start_matches(char::is_whitespace)
            .trim_end()
            == "/*"
            && line_after_directive.trim() == "*/";

    if is_standalone_comment {
        Fix::delete(Span::new(line_start as u32, line_end as u32)).with_kind(FixKind::Suggestion)
    } else {
        Fix::delete(span).with_kind(FixKind::Suggestion)
    }
}

   331	fn build_unused_disable_diagnostic_report(
   332	    message: String,
   333	    span: Span,
   334	    severity: DiagnosticSeverity,
   335	    source_text: &str,
   336	    rope: &Rope,
   337	    fix: Option<&Fix>,
   338	) -> DiagnosticReport {
   339	    let start_position = offset_to_position(rope, span.start, source_text);
   340	    let end_position = offset_to_position(rope, span.end, source_text);
   341	    let range = Range::new(start_position, end_position);
   342	
   343	    DiagnosticReport {
   344	        diagnostic: Diagnostic {
   345	            range,
   346	            severity: Some(severity),
   347	            code: Some("".into()),
   348	            message,
   349	            source: Some("oxc".into()),
   350	            code_description: None,
   351	            related_information: None,
   352	            tags: None,
   353	            data: None,
   354	        },
   355	        code_action: fix.map(|fix| LinterCodeAction {
   356	            range,
   357	            fixed_content: vec![fix_to_fixed_content(
   358	                fix,
   359	                rope,
   360	                source_text,
   361	                FixedContentKind::UnusedDirective,
   362	            )],
   363	        }),
   364	    }
   365	}
   366	
   367	/// Create a deletion fix for an unused disable directive.
   368	///
   369	/// Disable directive spans point at the comment content (for example, the
   370	/// `oxlint-disable ...` part of `// oxlint-disable ...`). Deleting that span
   371	/// directly leaves behind empty comment delimiters (`//` or `/**/`). When the
   372	/// directive is the only meaningful content on its line, expand the fix to the
   373	/// whole line so editor fix-all removes the noisy empty comment entirely.
   374	fn unused_directive_delete_fix(source_text: &str, span: Span) -> Fix {
   375	    let start = span.start as usize;
   376	    let end = span.end as usize;
   377	
   378	    let line_start = source_text[..start].rfind('\n').map_or(0, |index| index + 1);
   379	    let line_end = source_text[end..].find('\n').map_or(source_text.len(), |index| end + index);
   380	    let line_end_including_newline =
   381	        source_text[end..].find('\n').map_or(source_text.len(), |index| end + index + 1);
   382	
   383	    let line_before_directive = &source_text[line_start..start];
   384	    let line_after_directive = &source_text[end..line_end];
   385	
   386	    // If the only non-whitespace tokens outside the directive span are comment
   387	    // delimiters, removing just the directive would leave an empty comment.
   388	    // Expand to the entire line in that case, including the newline when there
   389	    // is one, so no blank line is left behind either.
   390	    let line_prefix = line_before_directive.trim_start_matches(char::is_whitespace).trim_end();
   391	    let line_suffix = line_after_directive.trim();
   392	    let is_standalone_comment = (line_prefix == "//" && line_suffix.is_empty())
   393	        || (line_prefix == "/*" && line_suffix == "*/");
   394	
   395	    if is_standalone_comment {
   396	        Fix::delete(Span::new(line_start as u32, line_end_including_newline as u32))
   397	            .with_kind(FixKind::Suggestion)
   398	    } else {
   399	        Fix::delete(span).with_kind(FixKind::Suggestion)
   400	    }
   401	}
   402	
   403	pub fn offset_to_position(rope: &Rope, offset: u32, source_text: &str) -> Position {
   404	    let (line, column) = get_line_column(rope, offset, source_text);
   405	    Position::new(line, column)
   406	}

str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/apps/oxlint/src/lsp/error_with_position.rs   --old_str '/// Create a deletion fix for an unused disable directive.
///
/// Disable directive spans point at the comment content (for example, the
/// `oxlint-disable ...` part of `// oxlint-disable ...`). Deleting that span
/// directly leaves behind empty comment delimiters (`//` or `/**/`). When the
/// directive is the only meaningful content on its line, expand the fix to the
/// whole line so editor fix-all removes the noisy empty comment entirely.
fn unused_directive_delete_fix(source_text: &str, span: Span) -> Fix {
    let start = span.start as usize;
    let end = span.end as usize;

    let line_start = source_text[..start].rfind('"'"'\n'"'"').map_or(0, |index| index + 1);
    let line_end = source_text[end..].find('"'"'\n'"'"').map_or(source_text.len(), |index| end + index);
    let line_end_including_newline =
        source_text[end..].find('"'"'\n'"'"').map_or(source_text.len(), |index| end + index + 1);

    let line_before_directive = &source_text[line_start..start];
    let line_after_directive = &source_text[end..line_end];

    // If the only non-whitespace tokens outside the directive span are comment
    // delimiters, removing just the directive would leave an empty comment.
    // Expand to the entire line in that case, including the newline when there
    // is one, so no blank line is left behind either.
    let line_prefix = line_before_directive.trim_start_matches(char::is_whitespace).trim_end();
    let line_suffix = line_after_directive.trim();
    let is_standalone_comment = (line_prefix == "//" && line_suffix.is_empty())
        || (line_prefix == "/*" && line_suffix == "*/");

    if is_standalone_comment {
        Fix::delete(Span::new(line_start as u32, line_end_including_newline as u32))
            .with_kind(FixKind::Suggestion)
    } else {
        Fix::delete(span).with_kind(FixKind::Suggestion)
    }
}

///
/// Disable directive spans point at the comment content (for example, the
/// `oxlint-disable ...` part of `// oxlint-disable ...`). Deleting that span
/// directly leaves behind empty comment delimiters (`//` or `/**/`). Expand the
/// fix to the full comment token, or to the whole line if the directive comment
/// is the only meaningful content on the line.
fn unused_directive_delete_fix(source_text: &str, span: Span) -> Fix {
    let start = span.start as usize;
    let end = span.end as usize;

    // `DisableRuleComment::span` is created from `Comment::content_span`, so it
    // begins immediately after `//` or `/*`. Include the delimiter too.
    let comment_start = start.saturating_sub(2);
    let is_block_comment = source_text[end..].starts_with("*/");
    let comment_end = if is_block_comment { end + 2 } else { end };

    let line_start = source_text[..comment_start].rfind('"'"'\n'"'"').map_or(0, |index| index + 1);
    let line_end = source_text[comment_end..]
        .find('"'"'\n'"'"')
        .map_or(source_text.len(), |index| comment_end + index);
    let line_end_including_newline = source_text[comment_end..]
        .find('"'"'\n'"'"')
        .map_or(source_text.len(), |index| comment_end + index + 1);

    let before_comment = &source_text[line_start..comment_start];
    let after_comment = &source_text[comment_end..line_end];

    if before_comment.trim().is_empty() && after_comment.trim().is_empty() {
        return Fix::delete(Span::new(line_start as u32, line_end_including_newline as u32))
            .with_kind(FixKind::Suggestion);
    }

    // If this is an inline directive, remove the whole comment token instead of
    // only the directive content. Include immediately preceding whitespace to
    // avoid leaving trailing spaces after code.
    let delete_start = before_comment
        .rfind(|c: char| !c.is_whitespace())
        .map_or(line_start, |index| line_start + index + 1);

    Fix::delete(Span::new(delete_start as u32, comment_end as u32)).with_kind(FixKind::Suggestion)
}
'

# Reproduce the LSP unused-disable deletion range calculation.

def fixed_delete_range(src, span_start, span_end):
    start, end = span_start, span_end
    comment_start = max(0, start - 2)
    is_block = src[end:].startswith('*/')
    comment_end = end + 2 if is_block else end
    line_start = src.rfind('\n', 0, comment_start) + 1
    line_end_rel = src.find('\n', comment_end)
    line_end = len(src) if line_end_rel == -1 else line_end_rel
    line_end_including_newline = len(src) if line_end_rel == -1 else line_end_rel + 1
    before_comment = src[line_start:comment_start]
    after_comment = src[comment_end:line_end]
    if before_comment.strip() == '' and after_comment.strip() == '':
        return line_start, line_end_including_newline
    delete_start = line_start + len(before_comment.rstrip())
    return delete_start, comment_end

def apply_delete(src, start, end):
    return src[:start] + src[end:]

cases = [
    ("// oxlint-disable no-console\nvar x = 'y';", 2, len("// oxlint-disable no-console"), "var x = 'y';"),
    ("/* oxlint-disable no-console */\nvar x = 'y';", 2, len("/* oxlint-disable no-console") - 2, "var x = 'y';"),
    ("var x = 'y'; // oxlint-disable no-console\n", len("var x = 'y'; //"), len("var x = 'y'; // oxlint-disable no-console"), "var x = 'y';\n"),
]

for src, start, end, expected in cases:
    fixed = apply_delete(src, *fixed_delete_range(src, start, end))
    print(repr(fixed))
    assert fixed == expected

def fixed_delete_range(src, span_start, span_end):
    start, end = span_start, span_end
    comment_start = max(0, start - 2)
    is_block = src[end:].startswith('*/')

    newline = src.find('\n', comment_end)
    line_end = len(src) if newline == -1 else newline
    line_end_including_newline = len(src) if newline == -1 else newline + 1

    after_comment = src[comment_end:line_end]
    if before_comment.strip() == '' and after_comment.strip() == '':

+/// Create a deletion fix for an unused disable directive.
+///
+/// Disable directive spans point at the comment content (for example, the
+/// `oxlint-disable ...` part of `// oxlint-disable ...`). Deleting that span
+/// directly leaves behind empty comment delimiters (`//` or `/**/`). Expand the
+/// fix to the full comment token, or to the whole line if the directive comment
+/// is the only meaningful content on the line.
+fn unused_directive_delete_fix(source_text: &str, span: Span) -> Fix {
+    let start = span.start as usize;
+    let end = span.end as usize;
+
+    // `DisableRuleComment::span` is created from `Comment::content_span`, so it
+    // begins immediately after `//` or `/*`. Include the delimiter too.
+    let comment_start = start.saturating_sub(2);
+    let is_block_comment = source_text[end..].starts_with("*/");
+    let comment_end = if is_block_comment { end + 2 } else { end };
+
+    let line_start = source_text[..comment_start].rfind('\n').map_or(0, |index| index + 1);
+    let line_end = source_text[comment_end..]
+        .find('\n')
+        .map_or(source_text.len(), |index| comment_end + index);
+    let line_end_including_newline = source_text[comment_end..]
+        .find('\n')
+        .map_or(source_text.len(), |index| comment_end + index + 1);
+
+    let before_comment = &source_text[line_start..comment_start];
+    let after_comment = &source_text[comment_end..line_end];
+
+    if before_comment.trim().is_empty() && after_comment.trim().is_empty() {
+        return Fix::delete(Span::new(line_start as u32, line_end_including_newline as u32))
+            .with_kind(FixKind::Suggestion);
+    }
+
+    // If this is an inline directive, remove the whole comment token instead of
+    // only the directive content. Include adjacent whitespace to avoid leaving
+    // trailing spaces after code or leading spaces before code.
+    let (delete_start, delete_end) = if before_comment.trim().is_empty() {
+        let delete_end = source_text[comment_end..line_end]
+            .find(|c: char| !c.is_whitespace())
+            .map_or(line_end, |index| comment_end + index);
+        (line_start, delete_end)
+    } else {
+        let delete_start = before_comment
+            .rfind(|c: char| !c.is_whitespace())
+            .map_or(line_start, |index| line_start + index + 1);
+        (delete_start, comment_end)
+    };
+
+    Fix::delete(Span::new(delete_start as u32, delete_end as u32)).with_kind(FixKind::Suggestion)
+}

     let (line, column) = get_line_column(rope, offset, source_text);
     Position::new(line, column)

# Reproduce the LSP unused-disable deletion range calculation used after the fix.

def fixed_delete_range(src, span_start, span_end):
    start, end = span_start, span_end
    comment_start = max(0, start - 2)
    is_block = src[end:].startswith('*/')
    comment_end = end + 2 if is_block else end
    line_start = src.rfind('\n', 0, comment_start) + 1
    newline = src.find('\n', comment_end)
    line_end = len(src) if newline == -1 else newline
    line_end_including_newline = len(src) if newline == -1 else newline + 1
    before_comment = src[line_start:comment_start]
    after_comment = src[comment_end:line_end]
    if before_comment.strip() == '' and after_comment.strip() == '':
        return line_start, line_end_including_newline
    if before_comment.strip() == '':
        rel = next((i for i, c in enumerate(src[comment_end:line_end]) if not c.isspace()), None)
        delete_end = line_end if rel is None else comment_end + rel
        return line_start, delete_end
    return line_start + len(before_comment.rstrip()), comment_end

def apply_delete(src, start, end):
    return src[:start] + src[end:]

cases = [
    ("// oxlint-disable no-console\nvar x = 'y';", 2, len("// oxlint-disable no-console"), "var x = 'y';"),
    ("/* oxlint-disable no-console */\nvar x = 'y';", 2, len("/* oxlint-disable no-console */") - 2, "var x = 'y';"),
    ("var x = 'y'; // oxlint-disable no-console\n", len("var x = 'y'; //"), len("var x = 'y'; // oxlint-disable no-console"), "var x = 'y';\n"),
    ("  // oxlint-disable no-console  code();\n", 4, len("  // oxlint-disable no-console"), "  code();\n"),
]

for src, start, end, expected in cases:
    fixed = apply_delete(src, *fixed_delete_range(src, start, end))
    print(repr(fixed))
    assert fixed == expected
PY

# Reproduce the LSP unused-disable deletion range calculation used after the fix.

def fixed_delete_range(src, span_start, span_end):
    start, end = span_start, span_end
    comment_start = max(0, start - 2)
    is_block = src[end:].startswith('*/')
    comment_end = end + 2 if is_block else end
    line_start = src.rfind('\n', 0, comment_start) + 1
    newline = src.find('\n', comment_end)
    line_end = len(src) if newline == -1 else newline
    line_end_including_newline = len(src) if newline == -1 else newline + 1
    before_comment = src[line_start:comment_start]
    after_comment = src[comment_end:line_end]
    if before_comment.strip() == '' and after_comment.strip() == '':
        return line_start, line_end_including_newline
    if before_comment.strip() == '':
        rel = next((i for i, c in enumerate(src[comment_end:line_end]) if not c.isspace()), None)
        delete_end = line_end if rel is None else comment_end + rel
        return comment_start, delete_end
    return line_start + len(before_comment.rstrip()), comment_end

def apply_delete(src, start, end):
    return src[:start] + src[end:]

cases = [
    ("// oxlint-disable no-console\nvar x = 'y';", 2, len("// oxlint-disable no-console"), "var x = 'y';"),
    ("/* oxlint-disable no-console */\nvar x = 'y';", 2, len("/* oxlint-disable no-console */") - 2, "var x = 'y';"),

]

    print(repr(fixed))
    assert fixed == expected

+/// Create a deletion fix for an unused disable directive.
+///
+/// Disable directive spans point at the comment content (for example, the
+/// `oxlint-disable ...` part of `// oxlint-disable ...`). Deleting that span
+/// directly leaves behind empty comment delimiters (`//` or `/**/`). Expand the
+/// fix to the full comment token, or to the whole line if the directive comment
+/// is the only meaningful content on the line.
+fn unused_directive_delete_fix(source_text: &str, span: Span) -> Fix {
+    let start = span.start as usize;
+    let end = span.end as usize;
+
+    // `DisableRuleComment::span` is created from `Comment::content_span`, so it
+    // begins immediately after `//` or `/*`. Include the delimiter too.
+    let comment_start = start.saturating_sub(2);
+    let is_block_comment = source_text[end..].starts_with("*/");
+    let comment_end = if is_block_comment { end + 2 } else { end };
+
+    let line_start = source_text[..comment_start].rfind('\n').map_or(0, |index| index + 1);
+    let line_end = source_text[comment_end..]
+        .find('\n')
+        .map_or(source_text.len(), |index| comment_end + index);
+    let line_end_including_newline = source_text[comment_end..]
+        .find('\n')
+        .map_or(source_text.len(), |index| comment_end + index + 1);
+
+    let before_comment = &source_text[line_start..comment_start];
+    let after_comment = &source_text[comment_end..line_end];
+
+    if before_comment.trim().is_empty() && after_comment.trim().is_empty() {
+        return Fix::delete(Span::new(line_start as u32, line_end_including_newline as u32))
+            .with_kind(FixKind::Suggestion);
+    }
+
+    // If this is an inline directive, remove the whole comment token instead of
+    // only the directive content. Include adjacent whitespace to avoid leaving
+    // trailing spaces after code or leading spaces before code.
+    let (delete_start, delete_end) = if before_comment.trim().is_empty() {
+        let delete_end = source_text[comment_end..line_end]
+            .find(|c: char| !c.is_whitespace())
+            .map_or(line_end, |index| comment_end + index);
+        (comment_start, delete_end)
+    } else {
+        let delete_start = before_comment
+            .rfind(|c: char| !c.is_whitespace())
+            .map_or(line_start, |index| line_start + index + 1);
+        (delete_start, comment_end)
+    };
+
+    Fix::delete(Span::new(delete_start as u32, delete_end as u32)).with_kind(FixKind::Suggestion)
+}
+
 pub fn offset_to_position(rope: &Rope, offset: u32, source_text: &str) -> Position {
     let (line, column) = get_line_column(rope, offset, source_text);
     Position::new(line, column)
